Al-Bāqillānī's Definition of ʿIlm and Abū Yaʿlā's Defense
Al-Bāqillānī defines ʿilm as 'knowledge of the known as it is'; Abū Yaʿlā defends and clarifies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of al-Bāqillānī's definition of ʿilm and explain Abū Yaʿlā's logical argument for the redundancy of the phrase 'as it is'.

Core Idea
The condition of correspondence is inherent to knowledge; dropping it from the definition does not change the meaning.

In this lesson, we examine the classical Ashʿarī definition of ʿilm (knowledge) by al-Bāqillānī and the insightful defense by the Ḥanbalī jurist Abū Yaʿlā al-Farrāʾ. Abū Yaʿlā argues that the phrase 'as it is' (ʿalā mā huwa bihī) is logically entailed by the concept of knowledge, and therefore can be omitted without loss. This lesson will guide you through the definition and the logical reasoning behind Abū Yaʿlā's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the definition
Find what is being defined (ʿilm) and al-Bāqillānī's definition: 'maʿrifat al-maʿlūm ʿalā mā huwa bihī'.
2
Analyze the components: genus and differentia
The genus is 'maʿrifa' (knowledge) and the differentia is 'ʿalā mā huwa bihī' (as it is). Understand that this is a correspondence condition.
3
Examine Abū Yaʿlā's logical argument
He argues that if the condition were absent, the knowledge would be ignorance. This shows the condition is inherent, so it can be omitted.
4
Evaluate the definition type
Is this a hadd haqiqi (real definition) or hadd lafzi? It is a hadd haqiqi because it describes the essence of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أ - العلم : العلم في اللغة : نقيض الجهل .. وعلمت الشيء، بمعنى: عرفته. أما في الاصطلاح؛ فقد عرفه الإمام أبو بكر الباقلاني، بأنه: «معرفة المعلوم على ما هو به». وقد انتصر لهذا التعريف أيضًا الإمام أبو يعلى الفراء ودافع على صحته، لكنه أشار إلى إمكانية التخلي عن عبارة 'على ما هو به' في التعريف دون أن يخل ذلك به، فقال: لو قيل معرفة المعلوم، ولم يقل 'على ما هو به'، كفى، ويكون ذلك تأكيدًا، لأن العلم لا يصح أن يتعلق بالمعلوم ويكون معرفة إلا على ما هو به، ولو تعلق به على ما ليس به كان جهلا وخرج عن كونه علما، فلهذا صح على قوله : معرفة المعلوم.
A - Knowledge (al-ʿilm): ʿIlm in language is the opposite of ignorance... and I knew the thing, meaning I recognized it. As for technical terminology, Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani defined it as: 'knowledge of the known as it is.' Imam Abu Yaʿla al-Farra also supported this definition and defended its validity, but indicated the possibility of dispensing with the phrase 'as it is' in the definition without harming it, saying: If one said 'knowledge of the known' and did not say 'as it is', it would suffice, and that would be an emphasis, because knowledge cannot pertain to the known and be knowledge except as it is; if pertained to it as it is not, it would be ignorance and cease to be knowledge. Hence his statement 'knowledge of the known' is valid.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of ʿilm (knowledge) by Imam al-Bāqillānī, a leading Ashʿarī theologian: 'knowledge of the known as it is' (maʿrifat al-maʿlūm ʿalā mā huwa bihī). This is a correspondence theory of knowledge: truth is alignment between the mind and reality. Abū Yaʿlā al-Farrāʾ, a prominent Ḥanbalī jurist, defends this definition but argues that the phrase 'as it is' is redundant. His reasoning is a logical argument: knowledge by its nature corresponds to the object as it is; if it did not, it would be ignorance (jahl). Therefore, saying 'knowledge of the known' implicitly includes the condition of correspondence. This is a precise logical point about the definition of a term: the differentia may be implicit in the genus.

Key Terms
العلم (al-ʿilm): Knowledge of the known as it is, i.e., a true belief that corresponds to reality. [Note: Ashʿarīs commonly adopt this definition; others like the Muʿtazila define it differently; in later uṣūl, ʿilm often means certain knowledge obtained from evidence.]
المعرفة (al-maʿrifa): Synonym for ʿilm in this context; recognition or knowledge. [Note: Some authors distinguish maʿrifa as a higher form of knowledge, but here it is synonymous.]
على ما هو به (ʿalā mā huwa bihī): As it is in reality, the condition of correspondence. [Note: Used in definitions of knowledge to emphasize objectivity; later some drop it as implicit.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is impossible to define ʿilm
B) Because ʿilm by its nature entails correspondence to reality
C) Because al-Bāqillānī retracted it
D) Because ignorance also involves correspondence

Key Takeaway
The definition of ʿilm as 'knowledge of the known' is valid because correspondence is inherent to knowledge; the added phrase is redundant but clarifying.

The Method for Defining Difficult Terms
Method for defining terms by clearing peripheries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of 'clearing the peripheries' to isolate the essence of a term in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
To define a term, first exclude everything it is not.

The author acknowledges that defining some terms can be difficult, so he offers a methodological approach: thorough investigation by which we distinguish the thing we want to define from what is not part of it. This lesson walks you through that method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target term
Start with the term you want to define. In the passage, the term is 'ilm (knowledge).
Choose a term that is central to your discipline.
2
List what the term is not
List all the concepts that might be confused with the term but are actually different. The author lists ignorance (jahl), doubt (shakk), conjecture (zann), and imitation (taqlid).
These are the 'peripheries' to be cleared.
3
Clear those peripheries
Show that each of those concepts does not fit the true meaning. For example, ignorance is a belief contrary to reality, so it cannot be knowledge.
This narrowing moves you toward the essence.
4
Observe what remains
After exclusion, what remains is the core meaning. The author concludes that knowledge is definitive cognition that corresponds to the requirement of the evidence.
This is the 'reality' (haqiqa) you seek.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار إلى عدم ضرورية الحد فيما كان حده متعسرا، قال: الرأي السديد عندنا أن نتوصل إلى درك حقيقة العلم بمباحثة نبغي بها ميز مطلوبنا مما ليس منه فإذا انتفضت الحواشي وضاق موضع النظر، حاولنا مصادفة المقصد جهدنا . مع فنقول : الجهل عقد يتعلق بالمعتقد على خلاف ما هو به والعلم خالفه في ذلك ويتميز عنه والشك والظن يترددان بين معتقدين وهو بخلافهما في ذلك، فلا يبقى إلا النظر في عقد يتعلق بالمعتقد على ما هو به، من مقلد ذلك في التصميم والاستقرار مع القطع بأنه ليس علمًا، والنظر في العلم الحق وما يتميز به عن عقد المقلد فليجرد الناظر فكره لمحاولة الميز بينهما، فإن استتب له ذلك، فقد أحاط بحقيقة العلم . فإن ساعدت عبارة سديدة في الحد حد بها، وإن لم تساعد اكتفى بدرك الحقيقة، ولم يضر تقاعد العبارة فليس كل من يدرك حقيقة شيء تنتظم له عبارة عن حده. ثم إن ابن عقيل الحنبلي ساق هو الآخر عددًا من تعريفات العلم، ثم نقضها كلها واختار تعريف العلم بأنه وجدان النفس الناطقة للأمور بحقائقها والحقيقة أن معركة تعريف العلم كبيرة بين العلماء، مع أن الأمر في موضوعنا أهون من ذلك كله، فنحن لا نريد بالعلم هنا سوى الإدراك القطعي المطابق لمقتضى الدليل، فلا يكون للدليل إلا مدلول واحد يدل عليه، ويكون هذا المدلول هو العلم الذي يؤخذ من هذا الدليل . ونحن لا نعني بالعلم هنا سوى العلم الاكتسابي الذي هو إنما وقع عن نظر واستدلال، ومعنى النظر والاستدلال ما يحصل العلم به عن ابتداء نظر وفكر وعلم الكسب على ضربين: عقلي وشرعي. فأما العقلي، فهو ما لا يفتقر إلى شرع مما لو نظر العاقل فيه وتدبره الحصل له العلم من غير شرع. وأما الشرعي، فهو العلم الواقع عن الكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة، والقياس على أحد هذه الأصول الثلاثة فما يؤدي النظر فيه إلى العلم يدخل فيه جميع أدلة العقول المتوصل بها إلى العلم بحقائق الأشياء وأحكامها وسائر القضايا العقلية، ويدخل فيه أدلة جميع السمع الموجبة للعلم والقطع من نصوص الكتاب والسنة، ومفهومها، ولحنها، وإجماع الأمة، والمتواتر من الأخبار، وأفعال الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام الواقعة موقع البيان، وكل طريق من طرق السمع يوصل النظر فيه إلى العلم بحكم الشرع دون غلبة الظن.
And he pointed to the lack of necessity of definition when its definition is difficult, saying: The correct opinion with us is that we arrive at the reality of knowledge through investigation by which we seek to distinguish our sought object from what is not part of it. So when the peripheries are cleared and the place of investigation narrows, we try to encounter the goal with our effort. So we say: Ignorance is a conviction related to the believed object contrary to what it actually is, and knowledge is opposite to it in that and distinguishes itself from it. Doubt and conjecture oscillate between two beliefs, and knowledge is contrary to them in that. So nothing remains except consideration of a conviction related to the believed object as it actually is, of the one who imitates it in determination and stability with the certainty that it is not knowledge, and consideration of true knowledge and what distinguishes it from the conviction of the imitator. So let the investigator free his mind for attempting the distinction between them. If that succeeds for him, he has encompassed the reality of knowledge. If a sound expression assists in definition, he defines by it; if not, he is content with grasping the reality, and the failure of expression does no harm, for not everyone who grasps the reality of a thing has a coherent expression for its definition. Then Ibn 'Aqil al-Hanbali presented a number of definitions of knowledge, then refuted them all and chose the definition of knowledge as 'the finding of the rational soul of matters as they truly are'. The truth is that the battle over the definition of knowledge is great among scholars, but the matter in our subject is easier than all that: we do not intend by 'knowledge' here except definitive cognition that corresponds to the requirement of the evidence. So the evidence has only one single indication that it indicates, and this indicated meaning is the knowledge taken from this evidence. And we do not mean by 'knowledge' here except acquired knowledge, which indeed occurs through investigation and inference. The meaning of investigation and inference is that through which knowledge is obtained by beginning with investigation and thought. Acquired knowledge is of two types: rational and legal. As for rational, it is what does not depend on revelation, such that if a rational person looks into it and reflects, he obtains knowledge without revelation. As for legal, it is knowledge that occurs through the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community, and analogy upon one of these three foundations. So what leads through investigation to knowledge includes all intellectual proofs by which knowledge of the realities and rulings of things and all rational propositions is reached, and it includes all revealed proofs that necessitate knowledge and certainty from the texts of the Book and Sunnah, their implication, their allusion, consensus of the community, widely transmitted reports, and the actions of the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him) that occur in the position of clarification, and every path of revelation that leads through investigation to knowledge of the legal ruling without predominance of conjecture.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion of 'ilm (knowledge) and its types. The author begins by acknowledging the difficulty of defining things whose definitions are problematic, then presents a method: thorough investigation that separates the defined thing from what is not it. He then defines knowledge by contrasting it with ignorance, doubt, and conjecture: ignorance is a belief contrary to reality, doubt and conjecture oscillate, while knowledge is a firm belief that corresponds to reality. True knowledge is distinguished from blind imitation (taqlid) by certainty. The author then mentions Ibn 'Aqil's definition of knowledge as 'the rational soul's finding of things as they are', but ultimately adopts a simpler, practical definition for the purposes of his discipline: 'definitive cognition that corresponds to the requirement of the evidence.' This restricts knowledge to what is acquired through investigation and inference (al-'ilm al-iktisabi). He then divides this acquired knowledge into rational ('aqli) and legal (shar'i). Rational knowledge is derived from intellect alone, without need for revelation. Legal knowledge comes from the Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. This division underscores that both rational and revealed sources lead to certain knowledge when properly investigated. The passage thus functions as a foundational definition for the work, clarifying what 'knowledge' means in the context of jadal and usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
العلم
الجهل
الظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

beginner
5 min
Distinguishing Knowledge from Ignorance, Doubt, and Conjecture
Contrasting knowledge with ignorance, doubt, conjecture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish 'ilm from jahl, shakk, and zann based on their definitions.

Core Idea
Knowledge is a firm belief that matches reality; ignorance is the opposite; doubt and conjecture oscillate.

The author contrasts knowledge with three other states: ignorance (jahl), doubt (shakk), and conjecture (zann). This lesson clarifies each concept so you can recognise them in arguments.

Guided Path
1
Define ignorance (jahl)
Ignorance is a conviction that is contrary to reality. For example, believing that intoxicants are permissible despite the clear prohibition.
It is the opposite of knowledge.
2
Define doubt (shakk)
Doubt is oscillation between two beliefs with no preponderance. For example, being unsure whether a hadith is authentic or weak.
Doubt is not firm.
3
Define conjecture (zann)
Conjecture is a preference for one belief over another, but without certainty. For example, thinking a particular ruling is likely correct based on a weak analogy.
It is stronger than doubt but less than certainty.
4
Define knowledge ('ilm)
Knowledge is a firm belief that corresponds to reality and is based on evidence. The author says it is 'definitive cognition' from the evidence.
It excludes doubt, conjecture, and error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار إلى عدم ضرورية الحد فيما كان حده متعسرا، قال: الرأي السديد عندنا أن نتوصل إلى درك حقيقة العلم بمباحثة نبغي بها ميز مطلوبنا مما ليس منه فإذا انتفضت الحواشي وضاق موضع النظر، حاولنا مصادفة المقصد جهدنا . مع فنقول : الجهل عقد يتعلق بالمعتقد على خلاف ما هو به والعلم خالفه في ذلك ويتميز عنه والشك والظن يترددان بين معتقدين وهو بخلافهما في ذلك، فلا يبقى إلا النظر في عقد يتعلق بالمعتقد على ما هو به، من مقلد ذلك في التصميم والاستقرار مع القطع بأنه ليس علمًا، والنظر في العلم الحق وما يتميز به عن عقد المقلد فليجرد الناظر فكره لمحاولة الميز بينهما، فإن استتب له ذلك، فقد أحاط بحقيقة العلم . فإن ساعدت عبارة سديدة في الحد حد بها، وإن لم تساعد اكتفى بدرك الحقيقة، ولم يضر تقاعد العبارة فليس كل من يدرك حقيقة شيء تنتظم له عبارة عن حده. ثم إن ابن عقيل الحنبلي ساق هو الآخر عددًا من تعريفات العلم، ثم نقضها كلها واختار تعريف العلم بأنه وجدان النفس الناطقة للأمور بحقائقها والحقيقة أن معركة تعريف العلم كبيرة بين العلماء، مع أن الأمر في موضوعنا أهون من ذلك كله، فنحن لا نريد بالعلم هنا سوى الإدراك القطعي المطابق لمقتضى الدليل، فلا يكون للدليل إلا مدلول واحد يدل عليه، ويكون هذا المدلول هو العلم الذي يؤخذ من هذا الدليل . ونحن لا نعني بالعلم هنا سوى العلم الاكتسابي الذي هو إنما وقع عن نظر واستدلال، ومعنى النظر والاستدلال ما يحصل العلم به عن ابتداء نظر وفكر وعلم الكسب على ضربين: عقلي وشرعي. فأما العقلي، فهو ما لا يفتقر إلى شرع مما لو نظر العاقل فيه وتدبره الحصل له العلم من غير شرع. وأما الشرعي، فهو العلم الواقع عن الكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة، والقياس على أحد هذه الأصول الثلاثة فما يؤدي النظر فيه إلى العلم يدخل فيه جميع أدلة العقول المتوصل بها إلى العلم بحقائق الأشياء وأحكامها وسائر القضايا العقلية، ويدخل فيه أدلة جميع السمع الموجبة للعلم والقطع من نصوص الكتاب والسنة، ومفهومها، ولحنها، وإجماع الأمة، والمتواتر من الأخبار، وأفعال الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام الواقعة موقع البيان، وكل طريق من طرق السمع يوصل النظر فيه إلى العلم بحكم الشرع دون غلبة الظن.
And he pointed to the lack of necessity of definition when its definition is difficult, saying: The correct opinion with us is that we arrive at the reality of knowledge through investigation by which we seek to distinguish our sought object from what is not part of it. So when the peripheries are cleared and the place of investigation narrows, we try to encounter the goal with our effort. So we say: Ignorance is a conviction related to the believed object contrary to what it actually is, and knowledge is opposite to it in that and distinguishes itself from it. Doubt and conjecture oscillate between two beliefs, and knowledge is contrary to them in that. So nothing remains except consideration of a conviction related to the believed object as it actually is, of the one who imitates it in determination and stability with the certainty that it is not knowledge, and consideration of true knowledge and what distinguishes it from the conviction of the imitator. So let the investigator free his mind for attempting the distinction between them. If that succeeds for him, he has encompassed the reality of knowledge. If a sound expression assists in definition, he defines by it; if not, he is content with grasping the reality, and the failure of expression does no harm, for not everyone who grasps the reality of a thing has a coherent expression for its definition. Then Ibn 'Aqil al-Hanbali presented a number of definitions of knowledge, then refuted them all and chose the definition of knowledge as 'the finding of the rational soul of matters as they truly are'. The truth is that the battle over the definition of knowledge is great among scholars, but the matter in our subject is easier than all that: we do not intend by 'knowledge' here except definitive cognition that corresponds to the requirement of the evidence. So the evidence has only one single indication that it indicates, and this indicated meaning is the knowledge taken from this evidence. And we do not mean by 'knowledge' here except acquired knowledge, which indeed occurs through investigation and inference. The meaning of investigation and inference is that through which knowledge is obtained by beginning with investigation and thought. Acquired knowledge is of two types: rational and legal. As for rational, it is what does not depend on revelation, such that if a rational person looks into it and reflects, he obtains knowledge without revelation. As for legal, it is knowledge that occurs through the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community, and analogy upon one of these three foundations. So what leads through investigation to knowledge includes all intellectual proofs by which knowledge of the realities and rulings of things and all rational propositions is reached, and it includes all revealed proofs that necessitate knowledge and certainty from the texts of the Book and Sunnah, their implication, their allusion, consensus of the community, widely transmitted reports, and the actions of the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him) that occur in the position of clarification, and every path of revelation that leads through investigation to knowledge of the legal ruling without predominance of conjecture.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion of 'ilm (knowledge) and its types. The author begins by acknowledging the difficulty of defining things whose definitions are problematic, then presents a method: thorough investigation that separates the defined thing from what is not it. He then defines knowledge by contrasting it with ignorance, doubt, and conjecture: ignorance is a belief contrary to reality, doubt and conjecture oscillate, while knowledge is a firm belief that corresponds to reality. True knowledge is distinguished from blind imitation (taqlid) by certainty. The author then mentions Ibn 'Aqil's definition of knowledge as 'the rational soul's finding of things as they are', but ultimately adopts a simpler, practical definition for the purposes of his discipline: 'definitive cognition that corresponds to the requirement of the evidence.' This restricts knowledge to what is acquired through investigation and inference (al-'ilm al-iktisabi). He then divides this acquired knowledge into rational ('aqli) and legal (shar'i). Rational knowledge is derived from intellect alone, without need for revelation. Legal knowledge comes from the Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. This division underscores that both rational and revealed sources lead to certain knowledge when properly investigated. The passage thus functions as a foundational definition for the work, clarifying what 'knowledge' means in the context of jadal and usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
العلم
الجهل
الشك
الظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of jahl (ignorance)?
A) Oscillation between two beliefs
B) A conviction contrary to reality
C) A firm belief corresponding to reality
D) Acquired knowledge from evidence

Key Takeaway
Knowledge is certain and matches reality; ignorance is the opposite; doubt and conjecture are intermediate states of uncertainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following as 'ilm, jahl, shakk, or zann: (a) Knowing that Allah exists after rational proof; (b) Thinking that a particular hadith is authentic after examining its chain, but still having some doubt; (c) Being unsure whether a certain act is obligatory or recommended; (d) Believing that wine is permissible despite the clear prohibition in the Qur'an.
?
Explain why the author says knowledge is 'contrary' to doubt and conjecture.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
5 min
The Author's Adopted Definition of 'Ilm
Author's adopted definition of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's definition of 'ilm and why it differs from other definitions.

Core Idea
For this discipline, 'ilm is definitive cognition that matches the evidence.

After presenting Ibn 'Aqil's definition and others, the author simplifies: knowledge here is only acquired definitive cognition from evidence. This lesson dissects that definition.

Guided Path
1
Recall the method of clearing peripheries
The author excluded ignorance, doubt, conjecture, and imitation to narrow down to the essence.
This method preceded the definition.
2
Identify the author's definition
The author says: 'definitive cognition that corresponds to the requirement of the evidence' (الإدراك القطعي المطابق لمقتضى الدليل).
This is the working definition.
3
Break down the definition: genus and differentia
Genus: 'cognition' (إدراك). Differentia: 'definitive' (قطعي) and 'corresponding to evidence' (مطابق لمقتضى الدليل).
This makes it a hadd (real definition).
4
Compare with Ibn 'Aqil's definition
Ibn 'Aqil: 'the rational soul's finding of matters as they truly are.' The author's is narrower, focusing on evidence and acquisition.
The author avoids metaphysical complexity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
5 min
Division of Acquired Knowledge into Rational and Legal
Division of knowledge into rational and legal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any piece of acquired knowledge as 'aqli or shar'i based on its source.

Core Idea
Acquired knowledge comes either from pure reason or from revelation.

The author divides acquired knowledge (al-'ilm al-iktisabi) into two types: rational and legal. This lesson explains the distinction and its importance in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define acquired knowledge
Acquired knowledge is that which is obtained through investigation and inference (iktisabi, as opposed to innate).
The author specifies that 'ilm here means this type.
2
Identify rational knowledge (al-'ilm al-'aqli)
Rational knowledge does not depend on revelation; a rational person can obtain it through reflection alone. Examples: existence of the Creator, mathematical truths.
It is a priori or deductive.
3
Identify legal knowledge (al-'ilm al-shar'i)
Legal knowledge comes from the Book, Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas) on these sources. It is derived from revelation.
It includes the methods of usul al-fiqh.
4
Recognise that both can produce certainty
The author says both types lead to 'ilm when properly investigated. Legal knowledge is not limited to zann; it can be certain (e.g., textual imperatives).
This contrasts with those who think only rational knowledge yields certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار إلى عدم ضرورية الحد فيما كان حده متعسرا، قال: الرأي السديد عندنا أن نتوصل إلى درك حقيقة العلم بمباحثة نبغي بها ميز مطلوبنا مما ليس منه فإذا انتفضت الحواشي وضاق موضع النظر، حاولنا مصادفة المقصد جهدنا . مع فنقول : الجهل عقد يتعلق بالمعتقد على خلاف ما هو به والعلم خالفه في ذلك ويتميز عنه والشك والظن يترددان بين معتقدين وهو بخلافهما في ذلك، فلا يبقى إلا النظر في عقد يتعلق بالمعتقد على ما هو به، من مقلد ذلك في التصميم والاستقرار مع القطع بأنه ليس علمًا، والنظر في العلم الحق وما يتميز به عن عقد المقلد فليجرد الناظر فكره لمحاولة الميز بينهما، فإن استتب له ذلك، فقد أحاط بحقيقة العلم . فإن ساعدت عبارة سديدة في الحد حد بها، وإن لم تساعد اكتفى بدرك الحقيقة، ولم يضر تقاعد العبارة فليس كل من يدرك حقيقة شيء تنتظم له عبارة عن حده. ثم إن ابن عقيل الحنبلي ساق هو الآخر عددًا من تعريفات العلم، ثم نقضها كلها واختار تعريف العلم بأنه وجدان النفس الناطقة للأمور بحقائقها والحقيقة أن معركة تعريف العلم كبيرة بين العلماء، مع أن الأمر في موضوعنا أهون من ذلك كله، فنحن لا نريد بالعلم هنا سوى الإدراك القطعي المطابق لمقتضى الدليل، فلا يكون للدليل إلا مدلول واحد يدل عليه، ويكون هذا المدلول هو العلم الذي يؤخذ من هذا الدليل . ونحن لا نعني بالعلم هنا سوى العلم الاكتسابي الذي هو إنما وقع عن نظر واستدلال، ومعنى النظر والاستدلال ما يحصل العلم به عن ابتداء نظر وفكر وعلم الكسب على ضربين: عقلي وشرعي. فأما العقلي، فهو ما لا يفتقر إلى شرع مما لو نظر العاقل فيه وتدبره الحصل له العلم من غير شرع. وأما الشرعي، فهو العلم الواقع عن الكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة، والقياس على أحد هذه الأصول الثلاثة فما يؤدي النظر فيه إلى العلم يدخل فيه جميع أدلة العقول المتوصل بها إلى العلم بحقائق الأشياء وأحكامها وسائر القضايا العقلية، ويدخل فيه أدلة جميع السمع الموجبة للعلم والقطع من نصوص الكتاب والسنة، ومفهومها، ولحنها، وإجماع الأمة، والمتواتر من الأخبار، وأفعال الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام الواقعة موقع البيان، وكل طريق من طرق السمع يوصل النظر فيه إلى العلم بحكم الشرع دون غلبة الظن.

This restricts knowledge to what is acquired through investigation and inference (al-'ilm al-iktisabi). He then divides this acquired knowledge into rational ('aqli) and legal (shar'i). Rational knowledge is derived from intellect alone, without need for revelation. Legal knowledge comes from the Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. This division underscores that both rational and revealed sources lead to certain knowledge when properly investigated. The passage thus functions as a foundational definition for the work, clarifying what 'knowledge' means in the context of jadal and usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
العلم العقلي
العلم الشرعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Acquired knowledge is either rational (from intellect) or legal (from revelation), and both can yield definitive knowledge.

Definition of Conjecture (Zann) and Its Relation to Evidence
Author defines conjecture and explains its relation to evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define conjecture (zann) as a preponderant belief with the possibility of its opposite, and identify its epistemological distinction from certainty (yaqin) and its figurative relationship to probabilistic evidence (amara).

Core Idea
Conjecture is not a weak belief but a preponderant one that still allows for the possibility of being wrong.

In Islamic logic and usul al-fiqh, the term zann (conjecture) occupies a crucial epistemological middle ground between doubt and certainty. The author carefully defines zann and explains how it relates to evidence. This lesson breaks down the definition and clarifies a common misunderstanding about the causal link between evidence and conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the Arabic term 'الظن' and its English equivalent 'conjecture'. Note that the author begins by stating a standard definition.
The term is discussed in the context of probabilistic evidence (amara).
2
Extract the genus (jins)
The definition places conjecture within the category of belief (i'tiqad). Identify 'اعتقاد' as the broader class to which conjecture belongs.
Belief is the shared genus with certainty (yaqin).
3
Extract the differentia (fasl)
Conjecture is distinguished by two features: preponderance (rajih) and the possibility of its opposite (ihtimal al-naqid). These separate it from doubt (equal possibility) and certainty (no possibility of opposite).
The differentia ensures that conjecture is not merely a supposition but a weighted belief.
4
Compare alternative definitions
The author also mentions that conjecture is 'one of the two sides of doubt with preponderance' and 'what results from an indicator'. These reinforce the same core idea.
The definition from al-Mufradat emphasizes the source (amara) rather than the epistemic state.
5
Understand the figurative relationship to evidence
The author clarifies that when he says evidence 'leads to' or 'indicates' conjecture, it is figurative. Conjecture arises at the sight of evidence initially, but not as a necessary causal result like decisive evidence causing certainty.
This nuance prevents misunderstanding the epistemological weight of amara.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - الظن : الظن : هو الاعتقاد الراجح مع احتمال النقيض . وقيل : الظن أحد طرفي الشك بصفة الرجحان . وفي المفردات: اسم لما يحصل عن أمارة . ونحن نريد بالظن هنا ما يقابل اليقين أي الاعتقاد الذي لا يكون جازما . فالظن معناه ترجيح أحد المعنيين أو المعاني التي يحتملها الدليل، باعتبار أن المعنى الذي تم ترجيحه له مستندات تقويه على المعنى المرجوح، فكان أحق بالتقديم عليه . ومرادنا بقولنا في هذا الضرب الذي يقع عند النظر فيه غالب الظن : إنه طريق للظن أو موصل ومؤذ إليه ؛ أنه مما يقع الظن عنده مبتدأ، لا أنه طريق كالنظر في الدليل القاطع الذي هو طريق للعلم بمدلوله، وإنما نتجوز بقولنا : يوصل ويؤدي،
B - Conjecture: Conjecture is the preponderant belief with the possibility of its opposite. And it is said: conjecture is one of the two sides of doubt with the attribute of preponderance. And in al-Mufradat: a name for what results from an indicator. And we intend by 'conjecture' here what is opposite to certainty, i.e., a belief that is not decisive. So the meaning of conjecture is the preponderance of one of the two meanings or meanings that the evidence can bear, considering that the meaning which has been preponderated has supports that strengthen it over the outweighed meaning, so it is more deserving of precedence. And our intended meaning in our statement concerning this type in which when investigating it, the predominance of conjecture occurs: that it is a way to conjecture or a means and indicator to it; that conjecture occurs at it initially, not that it is a way like the investigation of decisive evidence which is a way to knowledge of its indicated meaning. Rather we speak figuratively in saying: it leads and indicates.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'zann' (conjecture) and clarifies its status in relation to evidence. The author begins with a standard definition: 'conjecture is the preponderant belief with the possibility of its opposite.' This distinguishes it from certainty (yaqin), which lacks such possibility. He then cites another definition: 'one of the two sides of doubt with the attribute of preponderance,' and mentions the entry in al-Mufradat (a lexicon) defining it as 'what results from an indicator (amara).' The author then gives his own working definition for the purpose of the book: conjecture is opposite to certainty, i.e., a non-decisive belief. He elaborates that conjecture involves preferring one of multiple possible meanings that an evidence can bear, based on supporting factors. Importantly, he clarifies that when he says a certain type of evidence 'leads to' or 'indicates' conjecture, this is figurative speech; it is not a causal relationship like decisive evidence that produces certain knowledge. Rather, conjecture arises initially at the sight of such evidence, but not as a necessary epistemic result. This distinction is crucial for understanding the epistemological weight of different types of evidence in usul al-fiqh and jadal.

Key Terms
الظن
اليقين
الأمارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Conjecture is the opposite of certainty but does not require evidence.

Key Takeaway
Conjecture (zann) is a preponderant belief opposite to certainty, and its relation to evidence is figurative, not causal.

Islamic Jurists' View on the Purpose of Definition
Contrasts Islamic scholars' view of hadd as mere distinction with Greek logicians' view as essence depiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Islamic jurists' view of definition (hadd as tamyiz) from the Greek logicians' view (hadd as taswir), and explain the terminological shift from hadd to ta'rif.

Core Idea
For Islamic jurists, a definition's purpose is not to depict essence but to distinguish – a pragmatic shift from Greek logic.

This lesson explores a foundational contrast in the concept of definition (hadd) between Islamic jurists and Greek logicians. Understanding this difference is crucial because it shapes how definitions are constructed and evaluated in Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh). The passage also clarifies the relationship between the terms hadd and ta'rif, which are often used interchangeably but have subtle historical nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing positions on definition
Locate the Greek logicians' view (and their Muslim followers) that definition aims at 'taswir al-mahdud' (depiction of the defined's essence). Then find the Islamic jurists' contrasting view that definition is merely 'tamyiz al-mahdud 'an ghayrihi' (distinguishing the defined from other things).
The passage explicitly says 'yakhtalifuna' (they differ), signaling a clear opposition.
2
Extract the key technical terms: taswir vs tamyiz
Notice that 'taswir' is associated with essence (haqiqah) and is the Greek philosophical goal. 'Tamyiz' is the pragmatic, functional goal of the Islamic jurists. These two terms represent different epistemologies of definition.
Taswir is rare in usul al-fiqh; tamyiz is central.
3
Understand the synonymy claim between hadd and ta'rif
The passage asserts that 'al-hadd wa al-ta'rif bi ma'na wahid' (hadd and ta'rif are synonymous). Earlier and later usulists both used hadd for definition, but contemporary scholars prefer ta'rif. The shift is a matter of convention, not substance.
Some later scholars do distinguish them technically, but here they are treated as equivalent.
4
Trace the historical shift from hadd to ta'rif
The passage notes that 'al-muhdithun wa al-mu'asirun' (modern and contemporary scholars) prefer the term ta'rif. This reflects a broader trend in Islamic sciences to move away from heavily philosophical terminology.
This is a terminological shift, not a conceptual change in the purpose of definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلماء الشريعة الإسلامية في هذا يخالفون أهل المنطق اليوناني ومن حذا حذوهم من الفلاسفة الإسلاميين الذين يقولون إن القصد من الحد هو تصوير المحدود وتعريف حقيقته، في حين اكتفى علماء الشريعة الإسلامية بأن الحد هو تمييز المحدود عن غيره فثبت - إذا - أن الحد والتعريف بمعنى واحد غاية ما هنالك أن القدامى من الأصوليين وحتى المتأخرين منهم جروا على إطلاق لفظ الحد على التعريف، في أن المحدثين والمعاصرين أصبحوا يفضلون إطلاق مصطلح التعريف بدلا من مصطلح الحد.
And the scholars of Islamic law differ in this from the people of Greek logic and those who follow them among the Islamic philosophers, who say that the purpose of the definition (al-hadd) is to depict the defined (taswir al-mahdud) and to define its reality (ta'rif haqiqatihi), whereas the scholars of Islamic law sufficed with the view that the definition (al-hadd) is merely distinguishing the defined from other than it. So it is established, therefore, that al-hadd and al-ta'rif are synonymous, except that the earlier usulists and even the later ones continued to apply the term al-hadd to al-ta'rif, whereas the later and contemporary scholars have preferred to use the term al-ta'rif instead of the term al-hadd.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage contrasts the Islamic legal scholars' view of definition with that of Greek logicians and their Muslim followers. The Greek-oriented logicians hold that the purpose of a definition (hadd) is to depict the essence (taswir) and define the reality of the defined. In contrast, the Islamic jurists see definition merely as a means to distinguish the defined from other things. The passage then clarifies that the terms 'hadd' and 'ta'rif' are effectively synonymous, though historically 'hadd' was used more by earlier usulists, while modern and contemporary scholars prefer 'ta'rif'.

Key Terms
الحد
التعريف
تصوير
تمييز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) To list all properties of the defined

Key Takeaway
Islamic jurists redefined the purpose of definition from essence-depiction to mere distinction, a pragmatic shift that influenced later usul terminology and practice.

Critique of Defining by Example Alone
Critique of Baydawi's definition of istiqra'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flaw in defining a logical term by example alone and apply criteria for a complete definition from the Islamic logical tradition.

Core Idea
Defining by example without essential attributes is like describing a fruit only by its color.

The author critiques al-Baydawi's definition of induction (istiqra') because it relies on a single example instead of stating the necessary characteristics that distinguish induction from other inferential methods. In this lesson, you will learn why a proper definition in the Islamic logical tradition must include the genus and differentia, and how this critique applies to usul al-fiqh reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the term 'istiqra'' (الاستقراء) in the passage. It is the term whose definition is being criticized.
2
Extract the example given
Al-Baydawi provides an example: witr prayer is performed on a riding animal, so it is not obligatory, based on induction of the obligatory. Write down the example.
The example is about usul al-fiqh methodology.
3
Evaluate whether the example alone suffices as a definition
Consider: does the example explain what induction is? The author says it fails because it does not state the essential attributes (sifat lazimah) that distinguish induction from other concepts.
A definition should provide genus and differentia, not just an illustration.
4
Identify the missing essential attributes
From the context, what attributes are necessary for induction? Think about: induction involves examining multiple cases, finding a common pattern, and deriving a general rule. The example only shows one application.
The author implies that al-Baydawi omitted these attributes.
5
Apply the critique to another Islamic science term
Choose a term like qiyas (analogy). Would defining it only by an example (e.g., wine intoxicates so nabidh is forbidden) be sufficient? Why or why not?
This step reinforces the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستقراء، مثاله الوتر يؤدى على الراحلة، فلا يكون واجبا، لاستقراء الواجب. فقد عرف البيضاوي الاستقراء بمثال له، ولم يبين صفاته اللازمة له التي يتميز بها عن غيره، وحتى المثال الذي ضربه لم يكن مثالاً مباشرًا وإنما كان مثالاً غير مباشر، فاستقراء أساليب الإيجاب في الألفاظ الشرعية هو الذي أفضى إلى إدراك أن الوتر ليس بواجب لأنه لم يثبت طلبه بهذه الأساليب.
Induction: its example is that witr is performed on the riding animal, so it is not obligatory, due to induction of the obligatory. So al-Baydawi defined induction by an example for it, and he did not explain its necessary attributes by which it is distinguished from others. Even the example he gave was not a direct example but rather an indirect example. For the induction of the modes of obligation in the legal texts is what led to the realization that witr is not obligatory, because its demand was not established by these modes.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage critiques a method of definition that relies solely on an example. The author points out that al-Baydawi defined 'induction' (istiqra') by providing an example from usul al-fiqh: the witr prayer is performed on a riding animal during travel, and therefore it is not obligatory, based on induction of what is obligatory (i.e., obligatory prayers are not performed on mounts). The critic argues that al-Baydawi failed to state the essential attributes (sifat lazimah) that distinguish induction from other logical processes. Furthermore, the example itself was indirect; it did not directly illustrate induction but rather a specific application of it, namely, inducing from the modes of obligation in Shariah texts that witr is not obligatory because its demand is not expressed in those modes. The passage highlights the importance of complete definitions over mere examples.

Key Terms
الاستقراء (al-istiqra'): Induction: reasoning from particular cases to a general rule. The author criticizes defining it solely by example without specifying its essential characteristics. [Note: In logic, istiqra' can refer to complete or incomplete induction; here it is used in the context of usul al-fiqh as a method of inference.]

Key Takeaway

The Method of Definition by Division
Author introduces definition by division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the method of definition by division and apply it to clarify a term's meaning by locating it within an exhaustive classification.

Core Idea
Definition by division clarifies meaning by showing where a term fits in an exhaustive taxonomy.

Not all definitions are concise verbal formulae. Sometimes the clearest way to define a term is to show its place within a complete classification. This lesson introduces definition by division (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim), a method used by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi to define 'ilm and zann.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term to be defined
Find the definiendum (e.g., 'ilm, zann) that the author intends to clarify through division.
2
List all possible elements in the set
Determine the complete set of categories that will be divided. For Al-Razi, the set is all ranks of perception (maratib al-idrak).
3
Ensure the division is exhaustive and mutually exclusive
Check that every possible case falls into one category and no case falls into two. Al-Razi's division into certain vs. non-certain, then further subdivisions, aims to be exhaustive.
4
Locate the definiendum within the division
Once the classification is laid out, the meaning of the term becomes clear by its position. For example, 'ilm is located as certain, correspondant, with a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعا : التعريف بالتقسيم : ومقتضاه أن يقوم المعرف بسبر عناصر جملة معينة حتى يصل إلى العنصر المراد تعريفه من بين عناصرها، فيتضح معناه في الذهن دون أن يحتاج إلى ضبطه في عبارة محددة . ومثاله، ما نجده عند الإمام فخر الدين الرازي في تعريفه لمصطلحي العلم والظن فهو لم يحدهمها بعبارة موجزة كما هو حال كل تعريف أو حد، وإنما سبر وقسم كل مراتب الإدراك حتى اتضح من بينها معنى كل من العلم والظن . . قال : إن حكم الذهن بأمر على أمر إما أن يكون جازما أو لا يكون. فإن كان جازما : فإما أن يكون مطابقا للمحكوم عليه أو لا يكون . فإن كان مطابقا فإما أن يكون لموجب أو لا يكون. فإن كان لموجب : فالموجب إما أن يكون حسيّا، أو «عقليّا» أو «مركبًا منهما، فإن كان «حسيّا»، فهو العلم الحاصل من الحواس الخمسة، ويقرب منه العلم بالأمور الوجدانية كاللذة والألم. وإن كان «عقليّا»، فإما أن يكون الموجب مجرد تصور طرفي القضية، أو لابد من شيء آخر من القضايا، فالأول هو «البدهيات»، والثاني «النظريات». وأما إن كان الموجب مركبًا من الحس والعقل فإما أن يكون من السمع والعقل فهو «المتواترات». أو من سائر الحواس والعقل وهو «التجريبيات» و«الحدسيات». وأما الذي لا يكون لموجب، فهو «اعتقاد المقلد» وأما الجازم غير المطابق فهو «الجهل» وأما الذي لا يكون جازمًا، فالتردد بين الطرفين إن كان على السوية فهو الشك، وإلا : فالراجح «ظن»، والمرجوح «وهم» . . . والنماذج من هذه الأنواع في التعريف كثيرة في كتب الأصوليين، يمكن لمن أراد مزيد أمثلة منها أن يقف عليها في مظانها من كتب علم أصول الفقه.
Fourth: Definition by division: Its import is that the definer investigates the elements of a certain set until he reaches the element intended to be defined from among its elements, so its meaning becomes clear in the mind without needing to capture it in a specific expression. Its example is what we find with Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his definition of the terms 'ilm and zann, for he did not define them with a concise expression as is the case with every definition or limit, but rather he investigated and divided all the ranks of perception until the meaning of each of 'ilm and zann became clear from among them. He said: The mind's judgment of one thing concerning another is either certain or not. If it is certain: then either it corresponds to the subject matter or not. If it corresponds: then either it is due to a cause or not. If it is due to a cause: then the cause is either sensory, or intellectual, or composed of both. If it is sensory, it is the knowledge obtained from the five senses, and close to it is knowledge of intuitive matters like pleasure and pain. If it is intellectual, then either the cause is merely the conception of the two ends of the proposition, or it must be another thing from among propositions. The first is the 'self-evident', and the second is 'theoretical'. And if the cause is composed of sense and intellect, then either it is from audition and intellect, and that is 'mutawatir reports', or from the other senses and intellect, and that is 'experimentals' and 'intuitives'. And that which is not due to a cause is 'the belief of a taqlid follower'. As for the certain but non-corresponding, it is 'ignorance'. As for what is not certain: if the hesitation between the two sides is equal, it is 'doubt'; otherwise, the preponderant is 'conjecture', and the preponderated is 'illusion'. And examples of these types of definition are many in the books of the usuliyyun; whoever wants more examples can find them in their sources in the books of usul al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage explains the method of 'definition by division' (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim). The author states that this method involves the definer examining all the elements of a given set until the element to be defined is identified among them, thereby clarifying its meaning in the mind without needing a precise verbal formula. The example given is from Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's classification of knowledge and opinion in his work al-Mahsul. Al-Razi did not define 'ilm and zann with concise expressions but instead divided the entire hierarchy of perception. He begins by stating that the mind's judgment (hukm al-dhihn) is either certain (jazim) or not. If certain, it is either in accordance with reality (mutabiq) or not (in which case it is 'ignorance', jahl). If in accordance, it either has a cause (mujib) or not (the latter is 'belief of a taqlid follower', i'tiqad al-muqallid). If it has a cause, the cause can be sensory (hissi), intellectual ('aqli), or composite (murakkab). Sensory causes yield knowledge from the five senses and include intuitive matters such as pleasure and pain. Intellectual causes are either requiring only the conception of the terms (tasawwur tarafay al-qadiyya) – these are self-evident (badihiyyat) – or requiring additional propositions – these are theoretical (nazariyyat). Composite causes combine sense and intellect: if the sensory component is hearing/sam' (i.e., transmitted reports) along with intellect, they yield mutawatir reports; if from other senses and intellect, they yield experimental (tajribiyyat) and intuitive (haddsiyyat) knowledge. The certain but non-corresponding judgment is jahl. Non-certain judgments are divided into doubt (shakk, when hesitation is equal), conjecture (zann, when one side is preponderant), and illusion (wahm, when one side is preponderated). The author concludes that many such examples of definition by division are found in usul al-fiqh works.

Key Terms
التعريف بالتقسيم
العلم
الظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main advantage of definition by division over a concise verbal definition?
A) It requires less effort.
B) It clarifies meaning without needing a precise verbal formula.
C) It is the only valid method in usul al-fiqh.
D) It avoids using Arabic terms.

Key Takeaway
Definition by division is a legitimate method that relies on exhaustive classification rather than a concise verbal formula.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a term from usul al-fiqh (e.g., 'ijma') and construct a definition-by-division for it by listing the types of scholarly consensus (silent vs. explicit, etc.).
?
Analyze Al-Razi's definition of 'ilm by drawing his full division tree and explaining why each branch is necessary.

Al-Razi's Classification of Certain Knowledge
Al-Razi's division of certain judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace Al-Razi's classification of certain knowledge and identify each subtype: sensory, self-evident, theoretical, mutawatir, experimental, and intuitive.

Core Idea
Certain knowledge is divided by its cause: sensory, intellectual, or composite.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi provided a detailed classification of knowledge by analyzing the nature of mental judgments. This lesson unpacks his division of certain judgments into categories based on correspondence and cause.

Guided Path
1
Start with the first division: certain vs. non-certain
Al-Razi first divides judgment into certain (jazim) and non-certain. Focus on the certain branch.
2
Within certain, check correspondence
If certain, it either corresponds to reality (mutabiq) or not (non-mutabiq = jahl). Only mutabiq is considered true knowledge.
3
For mutabiq, check if there is a cause
If there is a cause (mujib), it is 'ilm; if no cause, it is taqlid (blind acceptance).
4
Classify the cause: sensory, intellectual, or composite
Sensory causes yield sense knowledge; intellectual causes yield self-evident (badihiyyat) or theoretical (nazariyyat); composite causes yield mutawatir, experimental, or intuitive knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعا : التعريف بالتقسيم : ومقتضاه أن يقوم المعرف بسبر عناصر جملة معينة حتى يصل إلى العنصر المراد تعريفه من بين عناصرها، فيتضح معناه في الذهن دون أن يحتاج إلى ضبطه في عبارة محددة . ومثاله، ما نجده عند الإمام فخر الدين الرازي في تعريفه لمصطلحي العلم والظن فهو لم يحدهمها بعبارة موجزة كما هو حال كل تعريف أو حد، وإنما سبر وقسم كل مراتب الإدراك حتى اتضح من بينها معنى كل من العلم والظن . . قال : إن حكم الذهن بأمر على أمر إما أن يكون جازما أو لا يكون. فإن كان جازما : فإما أن يكون مطابقا للمحكوم عليه أو لا يكون . فإن كان مطابقا فإما أن يكون لموجب أو لا يكون. فإن كان لموجب : فالموجب إما أن يكون حسيّا، أو «عقليّا» أو «مركبًا منهما، فإن كان «حسيّا»، فهو العلم الحاصل من الحواس الخمسة، ويقرب منه العلم بالأمور الوجدانية كاللذة والألم. وإن كان «عقليّا»، فإما أن يكون الموجب مجرد تصور طرفي القضية، أو لابد من شيء آخر من القضايا، فالأول هو «البدهيات»، والثاني «النظريات». وأما إن كان الموجب مركبًا من الحس والعقل فإما أن يكون من السمع والعقل فهو «المتواترات». أو من سائر الحواس والعقل وهو «التجريبيات» و«الحدسيات». وأما الذي لا يكون لموجب، فهو «اعتقاد المقلد» وأما الجازم غير المطابق فهو «الجهل» وأما الذي لا يكون جازمًا، فالتردد بين الطرفين إن كان على السوية فهو الشك، وإلا : فالراجح «ظن»، والمرجوح «وهم» . . . والنماذج من هذه الأنواع في التعريف كثيرة في كتب الأصوليين، يمكن لمن أراد مزيد أمثلة منها أن يقف عليها في مظانها من كتب علم أصول الفقه.
Fourth: Definition by division: Its import is that the definer investigates the elements of a certain set until he reaches the element intended to be defined from among its elements, so its meaning becomes clear in the mind without needing to capture it in a specific expression. Its example is what we find with Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his definition of the terms 'ilm and zann, for he did not define them with a concise expression as is the case with every definition or limit, but rather he investigated and divided all the ranks of perception until the meaning of each of 'ilm and zann became clear from among them. He said: The mind's judgment of one thing concerning another is either certain or not. If it is certain: then either it corresponds to the subject matter or not. If it corresponds: then either it is due to a cause or not. If it is due to a cause: then the cause is either sensory, or intellectual, or composed of both. If it is sensory, it is the knowledge obtained from the five senses, and close to it is knowledge of intuitive matters like pleasure and pain. If it is intellectual, then either the cause is merely the conception of the two ends of the proposition, or it must be another thing from among propositions. The first is the 'self-evident', and the second is 'theoretical'. And if the cause is composed of sense and intellect, then either it is from audition and intellect, and that is 'mutawatir reports', or from the other senses and intellect, and that is 'experimentals' and 'intuitives'. And that which is not due to a cause is 'the belief of a taqlid follower'. As for the certain but non-corresponding, it is 'ignorance'. As for what is not certain: if the hesitation between the two sides is equal, it is 'doubt'; otherwise, the preponderant is 'conjecture', and the preponderated is 'illusion'. And examples of these types of definition are many in the books of the usuliyyun; whoever wants more examples can find them in their sources in the books of usul al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage explains the method of 'definition by division' (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim). The author states that this method involves the definer examining all the elements of a given set until the element to be defined is identified among them, thereby clarifying its meaning in the mind without needing a precise verbal formula. The example given is from Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's classification of knowledge and opinion in his work al-Mahsul. Al-Razi did not define 'ilm and zann with concise expressions but instead divided the entire hierarchy of perception. He begins by stating that the mind's judgment (hukm al-dhihn) is either certain (jazim) or not. If certain, it is either in accordance with reality (mutabiq) or not (in which case it is 'ignorance', jahl). If in accordance, it either has a cause (mujib) or not (the latter is 'belief of a taqlid follower', i'tiqad al-muqallid). If it has a cause, the cause can be sensory (hissi), intellectual ('aqli), or composite (murakkab). Sensory causes yield knowledge from the five senses and include intuitive matters such as pleasure and pain. Intellectual causes are either requiring only the conception of the terms (tasawwur tarafay al-qadiyya) – these are self-evident (badihiyyat) – or requiring additional propositions – these are theoretical (nazariyyat). Composite causes combine sense and intellect: if the sensory component is hearing/sam' (i.e., transmitted reports) along with intellect, they yield mutawatir reports; if from other senses and intellect, they yield experimental (tajribiyyat) and intuitive (haddsiyyat) knowledge. The certain but non-corresponding judgment is jahl. Non-certain judgments are divided into doubt (shakk, when hesitation is equal), conjecture (zann, when one side is preponderant), and illusion (wahm, when one side is preponderated). The author concludes that many such examples of definition by division are found in usul al-fiqh works.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi defines 'ilm as certain, correspondant judgment that has a justifying cause, and he exhaustively classifies the types of such causes.

Al-Razi's Classification of Non-Certain Judgments
Al-Razi's division of non-certain judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish among doubt (shakk), conjecture (zann), and illusion (wahm) based on the strength of hesitation in a non-certain judgment.

Core Idea
Non-certain judgments are divided by the balance of hesitation: equal leads to doubt, imbalance gives conjecture and illusion.

After classifying certain knowledge, Al-Razi turns to judgments that are not certain. This lesson explains his tripartite division of opinion based on equality or imbalance of hesitation between two sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify non-certain judgments
These are judgments where the mind does not reach certainty (ghayr jazim).
2
Check the hesitation between the two sides
If hesitation is exactly equal, it is shakk (doubt). If one side is stronger, it is zann (conjecture) for the stronger side and wahm (illusion) for the weaker side.
3
Apply to examples
For instance, if a jurist is unsure about a ruling but feels one opinion is more likely, that is zann; the less likely is wahm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Linguistic and Early Terminological Definitions of Istidlal
Author presents the linguistic and early terminological definitions of istidlal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and compare the linguistic and early terminological definitions of istidlal given by al-Baji, al-Shirazi, and Ibn 'Aqil.

Core Idea
Istidlal is not merely 'seeking a proof' but an active following of the proof to reach the ruling.

In this lesson, you will explore how the term istidlal was defined linguistically and how early usul scholars like al-Baji and Ibn 'Aqil expanded on that definition. Understanding this foundation is crucial because it reveals the original breadth of the term, before later scholars restricted it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic origin
The term istidlal is derived from the root 'dalla yadullu'. Note that the linguistic meaning is simply 'seeking the proof' (talab al-dalil). Recognize that the form 'istif'al' indicates seeking.
2
Understand al-Baji's definition
Al-Baji defined istidlal as 'being guided by the proof and following its trace until one reaches the ruling'. This is an active process, not just seeking. Identify the key elements: being guided (al-ih tidal'), following (al-iqtifa'), and the goal (reaching the ruling).
3
Compare with simpler definitions
Other scholars like al-Shirazi, al-Farra', al-Sam'ani, and al-Tufi defined istidlal simply as 'seeking the proof' (talab al-dalil). Notice that these definitions are shorter and do not include the process of following.
4
Analyze Ibn 'Aqil's justification
Ibn 'Aqil supports the simpler definition by analogizing istidlal to other 'istif'al' words like isti'lam (seeking knowledge) and istikhbar (seeking information). He argues that the pattern indicates seeking. Understand this linguistic analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الأول : مفهومه عند الأصوليين
أ - الاستدلال لغة واصطلاحًا
الاستدلال لغة، استفعال من دل يدل، ومقتضاه بحسب اللغة؛ طلب الدليل. في الاصطلاح، فعرفه الباجي بأنه الاهتداء بالدليل والاقتفاء لأثره حتى يوصل إلى الحكم. وقد عرف كل من أبي إسحاق الشيرازي وأبي يعلى الفراء وأبي مظفر السمعاني ونجم الدين الطوفي الاستدلال بأنه «طلب الدليل». وقال ابن عقيل موافقا : اعلم أن الاستدلال؛ الطلب للدلالة على المعنى. وقال في موضع آخر مبررًا ومؤكدا الانتصار لهذا التعريف: «كما أن الاستعلام طلب العلم، وكما أن الاستخبار : طلب الخبر، والاستفهام: طلب الفهم، والاستنطاق : طلب النطق والاستشهاد طلب الشهادة، والاستخراج: طلب الخروج والاستحضار طلب الحضور والاستنصار: طلب النصرة، فالاستدلال : طلب الدليل، والله أعلم. وهو يطلق على فعل السائل وهو مطالبته المسؤول بإقامة الدليل، ويقع على المسؤول لأنه يطلب الدليل من الأصول. وقد ذهب الطوفي إلى أن الاستدلال هو طلب الدليل مطلقا سواء كان دليلا نقليًا أو عقليا ، فقال عنه : «هو طلب الحكم بالدليل من نص أو إجماع أو قياس . وقد يطلق الاستدلال على ما أمكن التوصل به إلى معرفة الحكم، وليس بواحد الأدلة الثلاثة». ويرى ابن النجار الفتوحي - على خلاف الطوفي - أن الاستدلال هو «إقامة دليل ليس بنص ولا إجماع ولا قياس شرعي ؛ فهو يخصه بالأدلة العقلية دون غيرها، بدليل أنه يدخل فيه كلا من القياس الاقتراني، والقياس الاستثنائي، وقياس العكس. أما الكفوي فينتصر لرأي الطوفي ويخالف ابن النجار، وذلك حين يقول في تعريف الاستدلال : يطلق في العرف على إقامة الدليل مطلقا من نص أو إجماع أو غيرهما، وعلى نوع خاص من «الدليل ولا خلاف في الحقيقة بين الفريقين، لأن الذين قالوا بانصراف الاستدلال إلى كل من النقل والعقل إنما أخذوا باصطلاح القدامى، والذين قالوا بانصرافه فقط إلى الأدلة العقلية إنما أخذوا باصطلاح المتأخرين الذين كانوا أكثر تأثرا بغلبة الفلسفة والمنطق على الفكر الإسلامي في الانحطاط . والاستدلال الذي نعنيه في بحثنا هذا هو إقامة الدليل، أو ما يسميه بعض العلماء (التقريب)، ويقصد به: سوق الدليل على وجه يستلزم المطلوب، فإذا كان المطلوب غير لازم واللازم غير مطلوب، لا يتم التقريب
The first topic: Its concept according to the usuliyyin. A - Istidlal linguistically and terminologically. Linguistically, istidlal is a verbal noun from 'dalla yadullu', and its implication according to language is 'seeking the proof'. Terminologically, al-Baji defined it as 'being guided by the proof and following its trace until one reaches the ruling'. And each of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, Abu Ya'la al-Farra', Abu Muzaffar al-Sam'ani, and Najm al-Din al-Tufi defined istidlal as 'seeking the proof'. Ibn 'Aqil agreed, saying: Know that istidlal is seeking the indication of meaning. And in another place he said, justifying and confirming his support for this definition: 'Just as isti'lam is seeking knowledge, and istikhbar is seeking information, and istifham is seeking understanding, and istintaq is seeking speech, and istishhad is seeking testimony, and istikhraj is seeking extraction, and istihdar is seeking presence, and istinsar is seeking victory, so istidlal is seeking the proof, and Allah knows best.' And it is applied to the action of the questioner, which is his demanding the respondent to produce the proof, and it occurs on the respondent because he seeks the proof from the sources. And al-Tufi held that istidlal is seeking the proof absolutely, whether it is a transmitted or rational proof, saying: 'It is seeking the ruling by means of a proof from text, consensus, or analogy. And istidlal may be applied to whatever can be reached by it to knowledge of the ruling, and it is not one of the three proofs.' And Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi, contrary to al-Tufi, holds that istidlal is 'producing a proof that is not text, consensus, or legal analogy; so he restricts it to rational proofs exclusively, evidenced by the fact that it includes both conjunctive syllogism, exceptive syllogism, and reversed analogy.' As for al-Kafawi, he supports al-Tufi's view and opposes Ibn al-Najjar, as he says in defining istidlal: 'It is used customarily to mean producing a proof absolutely, whether from text, consensus, or other, and also a special type of proof. And there is no real disagreement between the two groups, because those who said that istidlal extends to both transmitted and rational took the terminology of the earlier scholars, while those who said it extends only to rational proofs took the terminology of the later scholars who were more influenced by the dominance of philosophy and logic over Islamic thought during the period of decline. And the istidlal that we mean in this discussion is the production of the proof, or what some scholars call 'taqrib', meaning: presenting the proof in a way that necessitates the desired conclusion. If the desired conclusion is not necessary and the necessary is not desired, the taqrib is not completed.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory exposition of the term 'istidlal' (reasoning/inference) as used by Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyin). The author begins by stating the topic and then proceeds to give the linguistic definition: istidlal is a verbal noun derived from 'dalla yadullu', meaning 'seeking the proof'. The terminological definitions of various scholars are then presented. Al-Baji defined it as 'being guided by the proof and following its trace until one reaches the ruling'—this emphasizes that istidlal involves an active following of the proof to achieve a result. Others, including al-Shirazi, al-Farra', al-Sam'ani, al-Tufi, and Ibn 'Aqil, defined simply as 'seeking the proof'. Ibn 'Aqil supports this by analogizing istidlal to other words of the same pattern like isti'lam (seeking knowledge) etc., arguing that the form 'istif'al' indicates seeking. The passage then distinguishes two usages: istidlal can refer to the action of the questioner who demands a proof, or to the respondent who seeks the proof from the sources (usul). A significant disagreement is then presented: al-Tufi holds that istidlal is absolute and includes both transmitted (naqli) and rational ('aqli) proofs, specifically mentioning text (nass), consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). He also notes that istidlal can refer to any means of reaching a ruling, not limited to the three proofs. In contrast, Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi restricts istidlal to rational proofs, excluding text, consensus, and legal analogy. He includes conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani), exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i), and reversed analogy (qiyas al-'aks). Al-Kafawi then reconciles the two views by attributing the difference to a shift in terminology: earlier scholars used istidlal broadly, while later scholars, influenced by philosophy and logic, narrowed it to rational proofs. The author concludes by stating the definition used in this work: istidlal is 'the production of the proof' or 'taqrib', meaning presenting the proof in a way that necessitates the desired conclusion. This last part emphasizes the logical requirement that the proof actually entails the sought ruling, otherwise the taqrib fails. The passage thus provides a comprehensive semantic analysis of a key term in usul al-fiqh and logic.

Key Terms
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): Seeking or producing a proof to reach a ruling; in early usul, includes all types of proofs. [Note: Early definition was broad; later restricted to rational proofs.]
الدليل (al-dalil): That which serves as a proof; can be textual (nass), consensus (ijma'), analogy (qiyas), or rational arguments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Baji define istidlal as?
A) Seeking the proof
B) Being guided by the proof and following its trace until reaching the ruling
C) Producing a rational proof
D) Demanding a proof from the respondent

Key Takeaway
The early usul scholars defined istidlal broadly as seeking or following a proof, encompassing both textual and rational evidence.

The Terminological Shift in Istidlal: From Broad to Narrow
Author presents the disagreement over the scope of istidlal and the reconciliation by al-Kafawi, followed by the author's own definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between al-Tufi and Ibn al-Najjar over the scope of istidlal and the historical reason for the shift from a broad to a narrow definition.

Core Idea
The meaning of istidlal shifted from including all proofs to being restricted to rational proofs due to the influence of logic and philosophy.

After exploring the early definitions, this lesson examines a key disagreement: does istidlal include transmitted proofs or only rational ones? Al-Tufi and Ibn al-Najjar represent two opposing views, and al-Kafawi reconciles them by pointing to a historical shift in terminology. The author then specifies his own definition of istidlal as 'taqrib'.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Tufi's definition
Al-Tufi defines istidlal as 'seeking the proof absolutely, whether transmitted or rational'. He explicitly includes text, consensus, and analogy. He also notes that istidlal can refer to any means of reaching a ruling, not just the three proofs. Recognize that his definition is broad.
2
Identify Ibn al-Najjar's definition
Ibn al-Najjar restricts istidlal to 'producing a proof that is not text, consensus, or legal analogy'. He thus limits it to rational proofs alone. Evidence: he includes conjunctive syllogism, exceptive syllogism, and reversed analogy. Notice his definition is narrow.
3
Contrast the two definitions
Al-Tufi includes naqli (transmitted) and 'aqli (rational) proofs. Ibn al-Najjar excludes naqli proofs. This is the core disagreement. Note that both agree on the linguistic meaning but differ on the technical scope.
4
Understand al-Kafawi's reconciliation
Al-Kafawi supports al-Tufi's broad view but explains that the difference is due to a historical shift. Early scholars used istidlal broadly; later scholars, influenced by philosophy and logic, narrowed it to rational proofs. Thus, both are correct according to their respective terminological contexts.
5
Examine the author's own definition (taqrib)
The author defines istidlal as 'the production of the proof' or 'taqrib', meaning presenting the proof in a way that necessitates the desired conclusion. He adds a logical condition: if the conclusion is not necessary from the proof, then the taqrib is invalid. This definition emphasizes logical entailment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الأول : مفهومه عند الأصوليين
أ - الاستدلال لغة واصطلاحًا
الاستدلال لغة، استفعال من دل يدل، ومقتضاه بحسب اللغة؛ طلب الدليل. في الاصطلاح، فعرفه الباجي بأنه الاهتداء بالدليل والاقتفاء لأثره حتى يوصل إلى الحكم. وقد عرف كل من أبي إسحاق الشيرازي وأبي يعلى الفراء وأبي مظفر السمعاني ونجم الدين الطوفي الاستدلال بأنه «طلب الدليل». وقال ابن عقيل موافقا : اعلم أن الاستدلال؛ الطلب للدلالة على المعنى. وقال في موضع آخر مبررًا ومؤكدا الانتصار لهذا التعريف: «كما أن الاستعلام طلب العلم، وكما أن الاستخبار : طلب الخبر، والاستفهام: طلب الفهم، والاستنطاق : طلب النطق والاستشهاد طلب الشهادة، والاستخراج: طلب الخروج والاستحضار طلب الحضور والاستنصار: طلب النصرة، فالاستدلال : طلب الدليل، والله أعلم. وهو يطلق على فعل السائل وهو مطالبته المسؤول بإقامة الدليل، ويقع على المسؤول لأنه يطلب الدليل من الأصول. وقد ذهب الطوفي إلى أن الاستدلال هو طلب الدليل مطلقا سواء كان دليلا نقليًا أو عقليا ، فقال عنه : «هو طلب الحكم بالدليل من نص أو إجماع أو قياس . وقد يطلق الاستدلال على ما أمكن التوصل به إلى معرفة الحكم، وليس بواحد الأدلة الثلاثة». ويرى ابن النجار الفتوحي - على خلاف الطوفي - أن الاستدلال هو «إقامة دليل ليس بنص ولا إجماع ولا قياس شرعي ؛ فهو يخصه بالأدلة العقلية دون غيرها، بدليل أنه يدخل فيه كلا من القياس الاقتراني، والقياس الاستثنائي، وقياس العكس. أما الكفوي فينتصر لرأي الطوفي ويخالف ابن النجار، وذلك حين يقول في تعريف الاستدلال : يطلق في العرف على إقامة الدليل مطلقا من نص أو إجماع أو غيرهما، وعلى نوع خاص من «الدليل ولا خلاف في الحقيقة بين الفريقين، لأن الذين قالوا بانصراف الاستدلال إلى كل من النقل والعقل إنما أخذوا باصطلاح القدامى، والذين قالوا بانصرافه فقط إلى الأدلة العقلية إنما أخذوا باصطلاح المتأخرين الذين كانوا أكثر تأثرا بغلبة الفلسفة والمنطق على الفكر الإسلامي في الانحطاط . والاستدلال الذي نعنيه في بحثنا هذا هو إقامة الدليل، أو ما يسميه بعض العلماء (التقريب)، ويقصد به: سوق الدليل على وجه يستلزم المطلوب، فإذا كان المطلوب غير لازم واللازم غير مطلوب، لا يتم التقريب
The first topic: Its concept according to the usuliyyin. A - Istidlal linguistically and terminologically. Linguistically, istidlal is a verbal noun from 'dalla yadullu', and its implication according to language is 'seeking the proof'. Terminologically, al-Baji defined it as 'being guided by the proof and following its trace until one reaches the ruling'. And each of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, Abu Ya'la al-Farra', Abu Muzaffar al-Sam'ani, and Najm al-Din al-Tufi defined istidlal as 'seeking the proof'. Ibn 'Aqil agreed, saying: Know that istidlal is seeking the indication of meaning. And in another place he said, justifying and confirming his support for this definition: 'Just as isti'lam is seeking knowledge, and istikhbar is seeking information, and istifham is seeking understanding, and istintaq is seeking speech, and istishhad is seeking testimony, and istikhraj is seeking extraction, and istihdar is seeking presence, and istinsar is seeking victory, so istidlal is seeking the proof, and Allah knows best.' And it is applied to the action of the questioner, which is his demanding the respondent to produce the proof, and it occurs on the respondent because he seeks the proof from the sources. And al-Tufi held that istidlal is seeking the proof absolutely, whether it is a transmitted or rational proof, saying: 'It is seeking the ruling by means of a proof from text, consensus, or analogy. And istidlal may be applied to whatever can be reached by it to knowledge of the ruling, and it is not one of the three proofs.' And Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi, contrary to al-Tufi, holds that istidlal is 'producing a proof that is not text, consensus, or legal analogy; so he restricts it to rational proofs exclusively, evidenced by the fact that it includes both conjunctive syllogism, exceptive syllogism, and reversed analogy.' As for al-Kafawi, he supports al-Tufi's view and opposes Ibn al-Najjar, as he says in defining istidlal: 'It is used customarily to mean producing a proof absolutely, whether from text, consensus, or other, and also a special type of proof. And there is no real disagreement between the two groups, because those who said that istidlal extends to both transmitted and rational took the terminology of the earlier scholars, while those who said it extends only to rational proofs took the terminology of the later scholars who were more influenced by the dominance of philosophy and logic over Islamic thought during the period of decline. And the istidlal that we mean in this discussion is the production of the proof, or what some scholars call 'taqrib', meaning: presenting the proof in a way that necessitates the desired conclusion. If the desired conclusion is not necessary and the necessary is not desired, the taqrib is not completed.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory exposition of the term 'istidlal' (reasoning/inference) as used by Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyin). The author begins by stating the topic and then proceeds to give the linguistic definition: istidlal is a verbal noun derived from 'dalla yadullu', meaning 'seeking the proof'. The terminological definitions of various scholars are then presented. Al-Baji defined it as 'being guided by the proof and following its trace until one reaches the ruling'—this emphasizes that istidlal involves an active following of the proof to achieve a result. Others, including al-Shirazi, al-Farra', al-Sam'ani, al-Tufi, and Ibn 'Aqil, defined simply as 'seeking the proof'. Ibn 'Aqil supports this by analogizing istidlal to other words of the same pattern like isti'lam (seeking knowledge) etc., arguing that the form 'istif'al' indicates seeking. The passage then distinguishes two usages: istidlal can refer to the action of the questioner who demands a proof, or to the respondent who seeks the proof from the sources (usul). A significant disagreement is then presented: al-Tufi holds that istidlal is absolute and includes both transmitted (naqli) and rational ('aqli) proofs, specifically mentioning text (nass), consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). He also notes that istidlal can refer to any means of reaching a ruling, not limited to the three proofs. In contrast, Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi restricts istidlal to rational proofs, excluding text, consensus, and legal analogy. He includes conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani), exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i), and reversed analogy (qiyas al-'aks). Al-Kafawi then reconciles the two views by attributing the difference to a shift in terminology: earlier scholars used istidlal broadly, while later scholars, influenced by philosophy and logic, narrowed it to rational proofs. The author concludes by stating the definition used in this work: istidlal is 'the production of the proof' or 'taqrib', meaning presenting the proof in a way that necessitates the desired conclusion. This last part emphasizes the logical requirement that the proof actually entails the sought ruling, otherwise the taqrib fails. The passage thus provides a comprehensive semantic analysis of a key term in usul al-fiqh and logic.

Key Terms
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): Seeking or producing a proof to reach a ruling; in later usul, restricted to rational proofs. [Note: In earlier usul, istidlal included transmitted proofs; later scholars restricted it to rational proofs due to influence of philosophy and logic.]
التقريب (al-taqrib): A term used by some scholars for istidlal, meaning presenting the proof in a way that necessitates the desired conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The definition of istidlal underwent a historical shift from including all proofs to being restricted to rational proofs, and the author adopts a definition that emphasizes logical entailment in the proof.
