Verbal Dispute on Dalil and Hujja
Author clarifies a verbal dispute on dalil and hujja.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the fuqaha' and mutakallimun's usage of dalil and hujja and explain why their disagreement is verbal, not substantive.

Core Idea
The dispute over dalil and hujja is terminological, not about inference.

Scholars sometimes disagree on word meanings, not on the underlying methods. This passage shows how fuqaha' and mutakallimun use 'dalil' differently, yet both are correct in their own context. Understanding this prevents false debates and helps you appreciate how Islamic sciences can share the same tools but with different labels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
The passage contrasts 'fuqaha'' (jurists) and 'mutakallimun' (theologians). Note their different concerns: mutakallimun seek certainty, fuqaha' often work with probability.
2
Extract each group's definition of dalil
For mutakallimun, dalil yields certainty (yaqin). For fuqaha', dalil includes any indicator that leads to a legal ruling, even if only preponderant opinion (zann). Write down both definitions.
The passage says fuqaha' call even probabilistic indicators 'dalil' because God obligates them to act on such.
3
Understand the reason for the fuqaha' usage
The fuqaha' are required by Shar' to follow preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) from sources like khabar al-wahid and qiyas. Hence they term these proofs 'dalil' and 'hujja' in a legal context.
4
Recognize the author's resolution
The author quotes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi: the dispute is lafzi (verbal), not affecting inference. Both groups agree on the validity of using such indicators; the difference is only what to call them.
The passage ends: 'the mukallaf is required to follow what the evidence indicates, whether certain or probable.'
5
Apply the distinction to other terminological disputes
Reflect on how similar verbal disagreements might arise in other Islamic sciences (e.g., 'ijma', 'qiyas'). The lesson: check whether disagreement is about words or substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحافظ أبو بكر الخطيب حمد الله قلت : وما غلط الفقهاء ولا المتكلمون، أما المتكلمون فقد حكوا الحقيقة في الدليل والحجة، وأما الفقهاء فسموا ما كُلِّفُوا المصير إليه بأخبار الآحاد والقياس وغيره مما لا يكسب علما وإنما يفضي إلى غلبة الظن دليلا، لأن الله تعالى أوجب عليهم الحكم بما أدى إلى غلبة الظن من طريق النظر فسموه حجة ودليلا للانقياد بحكم الشرع إلى موجبه، وقد قيل: إنما سموا ما أفضى إلى غلبة الظن دليلا وحجة في أعيان المسائل لأنه في الجملة معلوم (أعني أخبار الآحاد والقياس، وإنما يتعلق بغلبة الظن أعيان المسائل، فأما الأصل فإنه متيقن مقطوع به» (1) . فالخلاف بين الفريقين لفظي، وليس له تأثير على الاستدلال، إذ أن كلا من الدليل والأمارة يستدل بهما ويتوصل بهما إلى معرفة الأحكام الشرعية أصولاً كانت أو فروعًا، والمكلف مطالب باتباع ما دل عليه الدليل سواء كان ما أفضى إليه قطعا أو ظنّا
Al-Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: 'By God, I say: The fuqaha' and the mutakallimun did not err. As for the mutakallimun, they stated the truth concerning evidence (dalil) and proof (hujja). As for the fuqaha', they called what they are obliged to resort to—such as reports of individuals, analogical reasoning, and other things that do not yield knowledge but only lead to preponderant opinion—evidence (dalil), because God Almighty obligated them to judge by what leads to preponderant opinion via the path of consideration; so they called it proof (hujja) and evidence (dalil) in submission to the ruling of the Law to its requirement. And it has been said: They only called what leads to preponderant opinion evidence and proof in particular cases because in general it is known (I mean reports of individuals and analogical reasoning); it is only the particular cases that pertain to preponderant opinion; as for the principle, it is certain and definitive.' So the dispute between the two groups is verbal, and it has no effect on inference, since both evidence (dalil) and indicator (amara) are used to infer and to arrive at knowledge of legal rulings, whether principles or branches; and the legally responsible person is required to follow what the evidence indicates, whether what it leads to is certain or opinion.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage clarifies a dispute between fuqaha' (jurists) and mutakallimun (theologians) about the terms 'dalil' and 'hujja'. The author quotes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who affirms that neither group is wrong. The mutakallimun correctly reserve 'dalil' for what yields certainty. The fuqaha' use the same term for indicators that yield only preponderant opinion (zann) because Shar'i obligations require them to act on such indicators. The author concludes that the disagreement is merely verbal and does not affect actual inferential practice: both types of evidence are used to reach legal rulings, and the mukallaf is obligated to follow what the evidence indicates, whether certain or probable.

Key Terms
الدليل
الحجة
غلبة الظن

Key Takeaway
